1 Introduction {#Introduction .indexable data-level="1"}				1 Introduction {#Introduction .indexable data-level="1"}
==============										==============

1.1 Overview {#Overview .indexable data-level="2"}					1.1 Overview {#Overview .indexable data-level="2"}
------------										------------

The scope of this Protection Profile ([PP](#abbr_PP)) is to describe the		The scope of this Protection Profile ([PP](#abbr_PP)) is to describe the
security functionality of operating systems in terms of [\[CC\]](#bibCC)		security functionality of operating systems in terms of [\[CC\]](#bibCC)
and to define functional and assurance requirements for such products.			and to define functional and assurance requirements for such products.
An operating system is software that manages computer hardware and			An operating system is software that manages computer hardware and
software resources, and provides common services for application			software resources, and provides common services for application
programs. The hardware it manages may be physical or virtual.				programs. The hardware it manages may be physical or virtual.

T.NETWORK\_ATTACK									T.NETWORK\_ATTACK
:   An attacker is positioned on a communications channel or elsewhere			:   An attacker is positioned on a communications channel or elsewhere
    on the network infrastructure. Attackers may engage in				    on the network infrastructure. Attackers may engage in
    communications with applications and services running on or part of			    communications with applications and services running on or part of
    the [OS](#abbr_OS) with the intent of compromise. Engagement may			    the [OS](#abbr_OS) with the intent of compromise. Engagement may
    consist of altering existing legitimate communications.				    consist of altering existing legitimate communications.

    on the network infrastructure. Attackers may monitor and gain access		    on the network infrastructure. Attackers may monitor and gain access
    to data exchanged between applications and services that are running		    to data exchanged between applications and services that are running
    on or part of the [OS](#abbr_OS).							    on or part of the [OS](#abbr_OS).

T.LOCAL\_ATTACK										T.LOCAL\_ATTACK
:   An attacker may compromise applications running on the				:   An attacker may compromise applications running on the
    [OS](#abbr_OS). The compromised application may provide maliciously			    [OS](#abbr_OS). The compromised application may provide maliciously
    formatted input to the [OS](#abbr_OS) through a variety of channels			    formatted input to the [OS](#abbr_OS) through a variety of channels
    including unprivileged system calls and messaging via the file			    including unprivileged system calls and messaging via the file
    system.										    system.

    having a limited amount of time with the physical device.				    having a limited amount of time with the physical device.

										      >	as for just-in-time compilation), then \"no exceptions\" should be
										      >	indicated in the assignment. Full realization of this requirement
										      >	requires hardware support, but this is commonly available. ]{.note}

										      >	    which attempts to allocate memory that is both writable and
										      >	    executable. The evaluator will run the program and confirm that it

::: {.appnote}									      <
[Application Note: ]{.note-header}[ ]{.note}					      <
										      <
Typically, the traffic required to establish the VPN connection is		      <
referred to as \"Control Plane\" traffic, whereas the [IP](#abbr_IP)		      <
traffic protected by the IPsec VPN is referred to as \"Data Plane\"		      <
traffic. All Data Plane traffic must flow through the VPN connection and	      <
the VPN must not split-tunnel.							      <
										      <
If no native IPsec client is validated or third-party VPN clients may		      <
also implement the required Information Flow Control, the first option		      <
shall be selected. In these cases, the [TOE](#abbr_TOE) provides an		      <
[API](#abbr_API) to third-party VPN clients that allows them to			      <
configure the [TOE](#abbr_TOE)\'s network stack to perform the required		      <
Information Flow Control.							      <
										      <
The [ST](#abbr_ST) author shall select the second option if the			      <
[TSF](#abbr_TSF) implements a native VPN client (IPsec is selected in		      <
[FTP\_ITC\_EXT.1](#FTP_ITC_EXT.1)). If the native VPN client is to be		      <
validated (IPsec is selected in [FTP\_ITC\_EXT.1.1](#FTP_ITC_EXT.1.1)		      <
and the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) is validated against the *[EP](#abbr_EP) for		      <
IPsec Virtual Private Network (VPN) Clients*), the [ST](#abbr_ST) author	      <
shall also include [FDP\_IFC\_EXT.1](#FDP_IFC_EXT.1) from this package.		      <
In the future, this requirement may also make a distinction between the		      <
current requirement (which requires that when the IPsec trusted channel		      <
is enabled, all traffic from the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) is routed through that	      <
channel) and having an option to force the establishment of an IPsec		      <
trusted channel to allow any communication by the [TSF](#abbr_TSF).		      <

[[ Evaluation Activities ]{.activity_pane_label}[]{.toggler}](#)		      <

[FDP\_IFC\_EXT.1](#FDP_IFC_EXT.1)						      <

::: {.eacategory}								      <
[TSS](#abbr_TSS)								      <
:::										      <
										      <
The evaluator will verify that the [TSS](#abbr_TSS) section of the		      <
[ST](#abbr_ST) describes the routing of [IP](#abbr_IP) traffic when a		      <
VPN client is enabled. The evaluator will ensure that the description		      <
indicates which traffic does not go through the VPN and which traffic		      <
does, and that a configuration exists for each in which only the traffic	      <
identified by the [ST](#abbr_ST) author as necessary for establishing		      <
the VPN connection (IKE traffic and perhaps [HTTPS](#abbr_HTTPS) or		      <
[DNS](#abbr_DNS) traffic) is not encapsulated by the VPN protocol		      <
(IPsec).									      <
										      <
::: {.eacategory}								      <
Tests										      <
:::										      <
										      <
The evaluator will perform the following test:					      <
										      <
-   **Test 1:**									      <
    -   **Step 1:** The evaluator will enable a network connection. The		      <
        evaluator will sniff packets while performing running			      <
        applications that use the network such as web browsers and email	      <
        clients. The evaluator will verify that the sniffer captures the	      <
        traffic generated by these actions, turn off the sniffing tool,		      <
        and save the session data.						      <
    -   **Step 2:** The evaluator will configure an IPsec VPN client		      <
        that supports the routing specified in this requirement. The		      <
        evaluator will turn on the sniffing tool, establish the VPN		      <
        connection, and perform the same actions with the device as		      <
        performed in the first step. The evaluator will verify that the		      <
        sniffing tool captures traffic generated by these actions, turn		      <
        off the sniffing tool, and save the session data.			      <
    -   **Step 3:** The evaluator will examine the traffic from both		      <
        step one and step two to verify that all non-excepted Data Plane	      <
        traffic in Step 2 is encapsulated by IPsec. The evaluator will		      <
        examine the Security Parameter Index (SPI) value present in the		      <
        encapsulated packets captured in Step 2 from the			      <
        [TOE](#abbr_TOE) to the Gateway and shall verify this value is		      <
        the same for all actions used to generate traffic through the		      <
        VPN. Note that it is expected that the SPI value for packets		      <
        from the Gateway to the [TOE](#abbr_TOE) is different than the		      <
        SPI value for packets from the [TOE](#abbr_TOE) to the Gateway.		      <
    -   **Step 4:** The evaluator will perform a ping on the			      <
        [TOE](#abbr_TOE) host on the local network and verify that no		      <
        packets sent are captured with the sniffer. The evaluator will		      <
        attempt to send packets to the [TOE](#abbr_TOE) outside the VPN		      <
        tunnel (i.e. not through the VPN gateway), including from the		      <
        local network, and verify that the [TOE](#abbr_TOE) discards		      <
        them.									      <

::: {.appnote}										::: {.appnote}
[Application Note: ]{.note-header}[Requesting a memory mapping with both	      |	[Application Note: ]{.note-header}[ ]{.note}
write and execute permissions subverts the platform protection provided		      |
by [DEP](#abbr_DEP). If the [OS](#abbr_OS) provides no exceptions (such		      |	Typically, the traffic required to establish the [VPN](#abbr_VPN)
as for just-in-time compilation), then \"no exceptions\" should be		      |	connection is referred to as \"Control Plane\" traffic, whereas the
indicated in the assignment. Full realization of this requirement		      |	[IP](#abbr_IP) traffic protected by the IPsec [VPN](#abbr_VPN) is
requires hardware support, but this is commonly available. ]{.note}		      |	referred to as \"Data Plane\" traffic. All Data Plane traffic must flow
										      >	through the [VPN](#abbr_VPN) connection and the [VPN](#abbr_VPN) must
										      >	not split-tunnel.
										      >
										      >	If no native IPsec client is validated or third-party [VPN](#abbr_VPN)
										      >	clients may also implement the required Information Flow Control, the
										      >	first option shall be selected. In these cases, the [TOE](#abbr_TOE)
										      >	provides an [API](#abbr_API) to third-party [VPN](#abbr_VPN) clients
										      >	that allows them to configure the [TOE](#abbr_TOE)\'s network stack to
										      >	perform the required Information Flow Control.
										      >
										      >	If the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) implements a native [VPN](#abbr_VPN) client,
										      >	then the [ST](#abbr_ST) author will select [provide a VPN client that
										      >	can protect all IP traffic using IPsec](#s-provides-vpnclient) and
										      >	includes the [PP-Module](#abbr_PP-Module) for [VPN](#abbr_VPN) Client as

										      >
										      >	In the future, this requirement may also make a distinction between the

Appendix B - Selection-based Requirements {#sel-based-reqs .indexable data-level="A"} <
=========================================					      <
										      <

requirements (those that must be performed by the [TOE](#abbr_TOE) or		      <
its underlying platform) are contained in the body of this			      <
[PP](#abbr_PP). There are additional requirements based on selections in	      <
the body of the [PP](#abbr_PP): if certain selections are made, then		      <
additional requirements below must be included.					      <

										      >	algorithm would require that \"[SHA](#abbr_SHA)-3-384\" be selected as a

										      >	[PP](#abbr_PP) Authors, and does not necessarily represent all such
										      >	dependencies in the document.
